ARIE 1959-1960 [vol. 078]


A.--COPPER-PLATE INSCRIPTIONS, 1959-60


ANDHRA PRADESH


KRISHNA DISTRICT


BANDAR TALUK


ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/1 (page )
Place
Masulipaṭṇam.--From the old collection in the office. Findspot: not known.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Kaliyuga 4902 (wrong for 4901), Śaka 1722, Raudri, Phālguna ba. 8, Sunday = 1801 A.D., March 8.
Language & Alphabet
Telugu
Remarks
Records the decision of the boundary limits and rules for irrigation of the villages Bāpaṭla and Cherkūru given by the collectors. Andrew Scott and John Read and I. L. Caldwell, the Superintendent of Tank repairs.

KURNOOL DISTRICT


NANDYAL TALUK


ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/2 (page )
Place
Nandyāl.--From the old collection in the office. Findspot: Nandyāl.
Dynasty
Chandravaṁśa
King
Vishṇuvardhana (?)
Date
Śaka 821 (wrong)
Language & Alphabet
Telugu
Remarks
Describes the king as the lord of Pāṭalāpura, and confers as inām the proceeds from the sale of the fish in the tanks Pāṇyaṁ-cheruvu, Rācha-cheruvu and Vaḍḍaguṇḍla-cheruvu on the bōyis who carry the god Pāṇikēśvara (in pro-cession) on the annual and other festival days. The record is in modern characters and is evidently a forgery.

SRIKAKULAM DISTRICT


PALAKONDA TALUK


ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/3 (page )
Place
Rājām.--Sri Pantula Visvanatha Sastri, Junior Deputy-Inspector of Schools. Through Sri V.S.Subrahmanian. Find-spot: Manthena, Srikakulam District.
Dynasty
Eastern Gaṅga
King
Anantavarman Chōḍagaṅga (?)
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Incomplete. Contains only the introductory part ending with the date of the coronation of Anantavarman Chōḍa-gaṅga in Śaka 999.

ASSAM


KAMRUP DISTRICT


ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/3-A (page )
Place
Gauhāṭī.--Copper-plate fixed into the left of the doorway of the innermost shrine (Chalantāmandir) of the Kāmākhyā temple.
Dynasty
Ahōm
King
Gaurīnāthasiṁha
Date
Śaka 1704, varṇa-ākāśa-muni-kshapā-kara.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Bengali Assamese
Remarks
Records the performance of Laksha-bali by Bṛihatphukkaṇa Haranātha, belonging to the Duvarā (Dvāra) family, on behalf of the king.

BIHAR


PATNA DISTRICT


ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/4 (page 34)
Place
Pātnā.--Impressions from Shri S.V. Sohoni, Commissioner. Through Dr. D.C.Sircar. Findspot: Katra, Muzaffarpur District.
Dynasty
Gupta of North Bihar.
King
Jīvagupta
Date
Year 2, Chaitra śu
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks
Issued from Tārā. Records the grant of the villages of Sura-bhākra, Yāmyā and Harigrāmaka in Tishṭihala-pāṭaka in the Chāmuṇḍa vishaya of Tīra-bhukti by the king in favour of the temple of the goddess Chāmuṇḍā-bhaṭṭārikā for the merit and fame of his father. In characters of about the 8th century A.D. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXV, pp. 125 ff.

BOMBAY


DEHGAM TAHSIL


ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/5 (page 34)
Place
Hilol.--Through Dr. H.D.Sankalia, Poona.
Dynasty
Rāshṭrakūṭa of Gujarāt.
King
Karka
Date
[Gupta-Valabhī] 470, Mārgaśira śu. 7, Monday = 788 A.D., November 10.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks
Issued from Harshapura by Vishayādhipati Mahāsāmanta Chandrāditya. Records the grant of lands in Pādāṭaka-grāma and Hilōhila-grāma to Bhaṭṭa Mātṛigaṇa, son of Mātrīśvara of the Kāśyapa-gōtra hailing from Sānanda. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXIV, pp. 213 ff.

AMRELI DISTRICT


AMRELI TALUK


ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/6 (page 34)
Place
Amrēli.--Amrēli Museum. Impressions through Dr. D.C.Sircar.
Dynasty
Maitraka
King
Kharagraha I
Date
Gupta-Valabhī 279, Śrāvaṇa śu. 10.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks
Issued from Valabhī. Records the grant of two vāpīs to the Brāhmaṇa named Gupta belonging to the Kauṇḍinya gōtra and Vājasanēya śākhā. The dūtaka was Dharasēna. Written by Sandhivigrahādhikṛita Divirapati Vatrabhaṭṭi. Published by A.S.Gadre in Important Inscriptions from the Baroda State, Vol. I, pp. 7 ff.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/7 (page 34)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Dhruvasēna II Bālāditya
Date
Gupta-Valabhī 323, Āshāḍha śu. 5.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks
Do. Records the grant of 150 pādāvarttas of land in one piece in the village, Machchhōtikā in Uttīrṇṇa-Ijjasthalī to Sōmaśarman, son of Śāmbakumāra-śarman. The dūtaka was Rājaputra Dharasēna. Written by Skanda-bhaṭa, son of Vatrabhaṭṭi. See Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXV, pp. 281 ff.

DHARI TALUK


ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/8 (page 34)
Place
Sarasiyā.--Plates in the possession of Shri R.N.Teckchandani; Forest Range Officer. Do. Findspot: Amrēli.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Śīlāditya III
Date
Gupta-Valabhī 368, Pausha śu. 1.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks
Issued from the jaya-skandhāvāra Pīṭupatraka-vāsaka. Records the grant of two pieces of land in the village of [Ajja]koṅha, one measuring 25 pādāvarttas and the other 100 pādāvarttas, the former with a well in it, in favour of Śaṅ-karaśarman alias Utarēśvara, son of Śankaraśarman of Bhāradvāja-gōtra and Bahvṛicha-śākhā, who hailed from Ānandapura. The dūtaka was Rājaputra Kharagraha. Written by Divirapati Śaṅkaragaṇa, son of Divirapati Hara-gaṇa. Ibid., pp. 281-82.

BARODA TALUK

Bhīma II

ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/11 (page 35)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Mūlarāja (I)
Date
Vikrama 1043, Māgha ba. 15, Sunday = 987 A.D., January 2.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the king's orders, issued from Aṇahilapāṭaka, grant-ing the village of Kambōikā in Mōḍhēraka ardhāshṭama in the Sārasvata-maṇḍala, on the occasion of a solar eclipse to the god Mūlanāthadēva, set up in the maṇḍalī in Varddhi-vishaya, for the merit of his parents and himself. The grant was written by Kāyastha Kā[ṁ]chaṇa. Ibid., No. 91.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/12 (page 35)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Bhīmadēva (II)
Date
Vikrama 1263, Śrāvaṇa śu. 2, Sunday, vyatī-pāta = 1206 A.D., July 9.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Damaged. Traces the king's genealogy from Mūlarāja I and records his orders, issued from Aṇahilapāṭaka, granting the village of Iṁdilā for the almhouses and cisterns attached to the temples of Bhīmēśvara and Līlēśvara at Līlāpura, which were built by queen Līlādēvī, daughter of Rāṇaka Samarasiṁha. The writer of the grant was Vōsarin, son of Kāyastha Ṭhakkura Kumāra. Ibid., No. 451.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/13 (page 35)
Place
Do. First plate of the set
Dynasty
Do.
King
Do.
Date
Vikrama 1287, Āshāḍha śu. 8, Friday. Irregular.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the king's grant of a village to the temples of Ānalēś-vara and Salakhaṇēśvara built at Salakhaṇapura by Sōluṁº (i.e. Sōlaṅkī) Rāṇaº Ānāū, for meeting the expenses of the temple and for feeding Brāhmaṇas in the feeding house of the place. Vēdagarbharāśi, the Sthānapati of Mūlēśvara-dēva-maṭha, was made the trustee of the grant. See Ibid., No. 486.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/14 (page 35)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Tribhuvanapāla
Date
Vikrama 1299, Chaitra śu. 6, Monday. Irregular.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Traces the king's genealogy from Mūlarāja I and records his orders issued from Aṇahilapāṭaka, granting, on the occasion of a solar eclipse in Phālguṇa, two villages called Bhāṁ-shara and Rājapurī to the feeding house created for the merit of the queen-mother Salakhaṇadēvī, in Talapada of Māula (?). The grant was written by Akshapaṭalika Ṭhakura Śōmasiṁha, son of Kāyastha Sātikumāra. The Dūtaka was Ṭhakura Vayajaladēva. A postscript declares Vēda-garbharāśi, the Sthānapati of śrī-Mūlēśvaradēva-maṭha (cf. No. 13 above) and his successors as permanent trustees. Another postscript makes the possessors of the granted vil-lages responsible for robberies committed in them. Ibid., No. 534.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/15 (page 36)
Place
The Director. Museum and Picture Gallery. Impressions through Dr. D. C. Sircar. Findspot: Kaḍī, Kadi Taluk, Mehsana District. First plate of the set.
Dynasty
Chaulukya (Vāghēlā)
King
Vīsala
Date
Vikrama 1317, Jyēshṭha ba. 4, Thursday = 1261 A.D., May 19.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the grant of 12 halas of land, 12 shops, etc., by Mahā-maṇḍalēśvara Rāṇaka Śāmantasiṁhadēva to feed Brāh-maṇas in the sattra of Āśāpalli, to maintain a cistern and to provide daily food-offerings and services and to get the repairs done in the temples of Ballālanārāyaṇa and Rūpa-nārāyaṇa, for the merit of the donor's grandfather Rānaka Lūṇarāja and father Saṅgrāmasiṁha. Rājakula Viśvāmi-trarāśi was made the trustee. Refers to the administration of the minister Nāgaḍa. The Dūtaka of the grant was Mahā-sāndhivigrahin Ṭhakura Śrīdhara and the writer was Mahā-kshapaṭalika Ma?? Gōvinda. Ibid., No. 557.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/16 (page 36)
Place
Do. Findspot: Jañjirā (Muruḍ Jañjirā), Kolaba District.
Dynasty
Śilāhāra
King
Apaṛājita
Date
Śaka 915, Vijaya, Śrāvaṇa ba. 15, Sunday, solar eclipse = 993 A.D., August 20.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit (verse), Nāgarī
Remarks
Traces the genealogies of the Rāshṭrakūṭas from Gōvinda I to Kakkala and of the Śilāhāras from Kapardin to Aparājita. Records the king's orders issued from Sthānaka granting a garden in the village of Sālaṇaka to the Brāhmaṇa Kōlama-kramavitta who was the son of Haradēva and belonged to Kāśyapa-gōtra and Bahvṛicha-śākhā, for his daily rituals. The donee is said to have hailed from Karahāṭa, to have been residing in Puṇaka-dēśa and to have come to Sthānaka on business. Refers to the minister Kēsapārya and to Sandhi-vigrahin Jhañjhamaiya. The writer of the grant was Kā-yastha Uddāma. son of Chakkaiya. Published by A.S. Gadre in Important Inscriptions from the Baroda State, Vol. I. pp. 55 ff.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/17 (page 36)
Place
Do. Findspot: Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Do.
Date
Do.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the gift of the village of Palachchha-uchchhika situated in Chikhkhalāḍavishaya in Purī-Koṁkaṇadēśa consisting of 1,400 villages, in favour of the Brāhmaṇa Kōlama-krama-vitta who was the son of Haridēva-gṛihītasahasra and belonged to Kāśyapa-gōtra and Bahvṛicha-śākhā. The record was written by Uddāma, son of Chakkaiya of Kāyastha-vaṁśa. when Ammaṇaiya was the Amātya or Mahāmātya and Jhaṁjha-maiya the Sandhivigrahin. The donee's family hailed from Karahāṭa-nagara. Ibid., pp. 46 ff.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/18 (page 36)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Chaulukya
King
Bhīmadēva II
Date
Vikrama 1283, Laukika Kārttika, Pūrṇimā, Thurs-day = 1226 A.D., No-vember 5.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the grant of the village Natāulī to the god Mūlēśvara at Maṇḍalī for daily worship and for feeding the ascetics in the matha. The gift was given over to Sthāvapati Vēda-garbharāsi. (cf. Nos. 13-14 above). Published in Ind. Ant., Vol. VI, pp. 199-200.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/19 (page 37)
Place
Do. Findspot: Bagumrā, Surat District.
Dynasty
Rāshṭrakūṭa
King
Nityavarsha (Indra III)
Date
Śaka 836, Yuva, Phālguna śu. 7.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks
Records the grant of the village Tenna near Kammaṇijja in Lāṭadēśa to Siddhapa-bhaṭṭa, who was the son of Venna-bhaṭṭa of Lakshmaṇa-gōtra and Vājimādhyandina-śākhā, on the occassion of the king's coronation. The king is stated to have made the grant while he was on the tulā-purusha at Kurundaka. The donee's family hailed from Pāṭaliputra. Trivikrama-bhaṭṭa, son of Nēmāditya wrote the praśasti. Published in JBBRAS, Vol. XVIII, pp. 253 ff.

ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/27 (page 37)
Place
Do. Findspot: Aṇastu, Karjan Taluk, Baroda District.
Dynasty
Rāshṭrakūṭa
King
Karkkarāja II
Date
Śaka 739, Vai-śākha śu. 15.,
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Issued from Kheṭaka-rājadhānī in Lāṭa-maṇḍala. Records the gift of the village of Majjā[s]taṇī in Bharukachchha-vishaya to the Brāhmaṇa Bhaṭṭa Śrībhaṭṭa who was the son of Kakkura, was a resident of Bharukachchha, belonged to the Vasishṭha-gōtra, and was a student of the Ṛigvēda. The dūtaka was Bhaṭṭa Drōṇamma and the writer was Nēmā-ditya, son of Kulaputra Durgabhaṭa. The grant ends with the endorsement svahastō mama śrī-Karkkarājasya śrīmad-Indrarāja-sutasya. Published by A.S.Gadre, op. cit., pp. 25-34.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/28 (page 37)
Place
Do. Findspot: Do.
Dynasty
Maitraka
King
Śīlāditya III
Date
Gupta-Valabhi 357, Māgha śu. 7.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Issued from the jaya-skandhāvāra of Dhānandā-vāsaka. Re-cords a gift of land to Balaśarman of the Upamanyu-gōtra who was a resident of Sraddhikā and whose family migrated from Girinagara. The gift land, in two plots, was situated in the village of Antikā in Bharukachchha-vishaya. A[na*]hila was the scribe and prince Dhruvasēna the Dūtaka. Ibid., pp. 16 ff.

The Dūtaka was Durggarāja and the writer Sāndhivigrahika Nārāyaṇa. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXII, pp. 77 ff.

BHAVNAGAR DISTRICT


BHAVNAGAR TALUK


ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/31 (page 38)
Place
Bhāvnagar.--Gāndhi Smṛiti (secured from the old Barton Museum).
Dynasty
Rāshṭrakūṭa of Gujarāt.
King
Prabhūtavarsha Gōvindarāja
Date
[Gupta]-Valabhī 500, solar eclipse.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Records a grant of a piece of land called Kōhala to the Brāh-maṇa Sōma of Śāṇḍilya-gōtra while the king was staying at Pālittānaka. The donee was the son of Karkka. The Dūtaka was Bhaṭṭa Śrīkumāra and the writer Jajjulla, the son of Padmanābha. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXV. pp. 269 ff.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/32 (page 38)
Place
Do. Findspot: Kaṭāpur, Mahuva Taluk, Bhavnagar District.
Dynasty
Maitraka
King
Dharasēna II
Date
Gupta-Valabhī 252, Vaiśākha ba. 15.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Records a grant of sixty pādāvarttas of land in the eastern border of the village of Dāmaripāṭaka situated in Vasha-palīka to the Brāhmaṇas named Viśākha and Bappa of Kāśyapa-gōtra. The record was written by Sandhivigrahā-dhikṛita Skanda[bhaṭa] and was issued from the camp at Bhadra[patta]naka. The Dūtaka was Chirbbira. Publish-ed in Prakrit and Sanskrit Inscriptions of Kathiawar, etc., pp. 35 ff.; cf. Bhandarkar's List, No. 1322.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/33 (page 39)
Place
Do. Findspot: Bōtāḍ, Botad Taluk, Bhavnagar District.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Dhruvasēna II Bālāditya
Date
Gupta-Valabhī 310, Āśvayuja ba. 15.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Issued from Valabhī. Records a grant of the village of Bha[sa]nta-grāma situated in Kālāpaka-pāṭhaka in Surā-shṭra. The purpose of the grant was to provide for the feeding, clothing and other requirements of the Bhikshu-saṅgha residing in the vihāra constructed by Gōhaka in the vihāra-maṇḍala created by queen Duḍḍā, and for effecting repairs to the vihāra. The Dūtaka was Sāmanta Śīlāditya. The record, written by Sandhivigrahādhikṛita Divirapati Vatra-bhaṭṭi, contains the endorsement sva-hastō mama at the end. Published in Ind. Ant., Vol. VI, pp. 13 ff.; cf. Bhandarkar's List, No. 1341.

ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/41 (page 40)
Place
Do. Findspot: Do.
Dynasty
Gārulaka
King
Varāhadāsa II
Date
Gupta-Valabhī 230, Māgha śu. 1.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Records that Mahāsāmanta Mahārāja Varāhadāsa (II) of the Gārulaka family, who was the brother of Mahārāja Śūra (II), the son of Sēnāpati Varāhadāsa (I) and the grandson of Mahārāja Śūra (I), made a gift of 100 pādāvarttas of land, probably in the possession of an agriculturist by name Ogghaka (Ogghaka-kuṭuṁbi-pratyaya-kshētra), in the village of Bhaṭṭipadra in order to provide for clothes and food for the nuns residing in the monastery of the merchant Ajita and for incense, lamp and oil for Lord Buddha. The charter was issued from Phaṁka-prasravara and the village Bhaṭṭipadra is described as situated near Phaṁka-prasravaṇa and as bestowed upon the chief by his Maitraka overlord Dhruva-sēna (I). The record states that Varāhadāsa (II) was lord of Dvārakā which he had acquired by his valour. The ecord, written by Bhaṭila, ends with the endorsement sva-hasta(tō)mama. Ibid., p. 79.

Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
The seal has Śrī-Bhaṭārkkah2. According to Mr. G.H.Khare, this spurious document states that 1400 hon (gold coins) were spent for getting an imperial farmān about something. BHUVANESWAR

Sōmavaṁśa
King
Mahābhavagupta I Janamējaya alias Dharmakandarpa.
Date
Year 34, Āśvina ba. 8.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Gauḍīya
Remarks
Issued from the victorious camp stationed at Suvarṇapura, the charter records the grant of a village called Konnayilla in the Ṭōkkārā vishaya of Kōśala-dēśa in favour of Bhaṭṭaputra Dēvu who was a son of Gāṅgēya and a grandson of Arjuna, and was an immigrant from Muktāvathi in Śrāvasti. Records the ratification of a grant, originally made by the king's uncle (pitṛivya) Dēvagaṇa, of a village in Purapaṭṭa-vishaya to Asaṅgaśarman, a Brāhmaṇa of the Dāṇḍāyana gōtra, Vājasanēya charaṇa and Mādhyandina śākhā for the merit of Dēvagaṇa. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXIV, pp. 169 ff.
ARIE/1959-1960/A/1959-60/65 (page 44)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Bābhaṭa

[Harsha] 83, Kārttika śu. 15.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks

ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/81 (page 52)
Place
Slab from the Ashṭabhujasvāmin temple at Site No. 29.
Dynasty
Ābhīra
King
Vasushēṇa
Date
Year 30, Va. pā 7, divasa 1.
Language & Alphabet
Prakrit, Brāhmī
Remarks
Records the installation, on the Sēṭagiri, of the image of Lord Ashṭabhujasvāmin by several persons, viz. Mahāgrāmika Mahātalavara Mahādaṇḍanāyaka Śivasēpa belonging to Kauśika-gōtra and the Pēribiḍēha [clan], the Yavanarājas of Sañjayapura. Śaka Rudradāman of Avanti and Vishṇu-rudraśivalānanda Śātakarṇi of Vanavāsa. Also records other pious acts apparently of the same persons such as decorating the enclosure [of the shrine of Ashṭabhujasvāmin] on the hill, cleansing of the well called Mahānandā, excava-tion of two tanks, one on the Sēṭagiri and another at Muḍērā. and planting of groves of palmyra trees. The engraver of the record was Vardhamānaka of the Sēṁbaka family. Amātya Tishyaśarman is stated to have composed the record. In characters of the 3rd or 4th century A.D. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXIV, pp. 197 ff.

ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/100 (page 53)
Place
Broken pillar found near Site No. 9
Dynasty
Ikshvāku
King
Ehavala Chāntamūla
Date
Year [8], Grīshma-paksha 4, di. [15].
Language & Alphabet
Prakrit, Brāhmī
Remarks
Damaged and fragmentary. Records the religious activities of an upāsaka named Chadasiri (Chandraśrī), described as the bestower of many religious gifts and as the performer of religious ceremonies in honour of the Buddha, Dharma and Saṁgha. The place where Chandraśrī performed the pious deeds recorded in the inscription is described as the Sethi-vara-vaḍhamāna (Śrēshṭhivara-vardhamāna) in the Mahā-nikāya of the Aparamahāvinaśailīyas at Vijayapura on the Śrīparvata. Also states that Chandraśrī made a sela-maḍava (śaila-maṇḍapa) and a bhara-sālā (bhaṁḍāra-śālā ?) for a particular Ariya-saṁgha (Ārya-saṁgha) with a view to attain-, ing nirvāṇa. Do. Ibid., pp. 7-10. Cf. A.R. Ep., 1958-59, No. B 84 which is also published in Ep. Ind., op. cit., pp. 9-10.
ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/101 (page 54)
Place
Panel of a lime-stone frieze depicting four principal events of the Buddha's life. From site No. 106 (Kumāranandi-vihāra).
Dynasty
Ikshvāku
King
Ehavala Chāntamūla
Date
Year 24, Varshā-pak-sha 4, di. 5.
Language & Alphabet
Prakrit, Brāhmī
Remarks
Damaged. States that the śaila-mayī pratimā of Bhagavat Buddha was installed at the Mahādēvī-parivēṇa at Vijaya-purī on the Śrīparvata by the śrēshṭhin Kumāranandin who was a son of Īśvaradatta and hailed from Syandaka-parvata. He is stated to have performed the meritorious deed along with his wife, his son Īśvarabhartṛi as well as his other kinsmen and relatives for the attainment of welfare and happiness for his own self and for all beings. Ibid., pp. 11-13.

ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/208 (page 66)

Suratrāṇa Mahimuda Pātasāha

ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/209 (page 66)
Place
Vaḍvā.--Right niche in the first storey of a step-well. Impressions from Dr. Z.A.Desai, Nagpur.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Vikrama 1539, graha-agni-bhūta-indu, Sādhāraṇa (for Saumya), Nabhasya (Bhādrapada) ba. 5, Monday. Irre-gular.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the construction of a step-well (vāpī) by Dhanada (Dhana, Dhanā, Dhanya or Dhanāka) of the Tāṁbūli (Tāṁ-bōlīya) varṇa for alleviating the distress due to drought. Dhanada was the son of Mukaṁda, grandson of Saihaḍa, great-grandson of Vijala and father of Balarāja. He belonged to the Mihara family (i.e. Mēr community) devoted to the goddess Nāgavallī and is credited with the performance of many charitable and religious deeds. His grandfather Saihaḍa also built many temples in honour of various deities at Stambhapura-tīrtha. The praśasti was composed by Hala who was a Nāgara-Brāhmaṇa. The step-well was constructed by Vanāka, son of sūtradhāra Rājā and Khētāka, son of sūtradhāra Dēvadāsa.
ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/210 (page 66)
Place
In the left niche of the first storey, same step-well.
Dynasty
Sult6ān of Gujarāt
King
Mahmūd Shāh Nas6īruddīn, son of Muh2ammad.
Date
Vikrama 1539, Bhādrapada śu. 8, Thursday = 1482 A.D., August 22.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Contains a praśasti recording the excavation of a step-well at Staṁbha-tīrtha by Mēhra Dhanāka (Dhana, Dhanā, Dhanya or Dhanada), son of Mēhra Mukaṁda. Mēhra (i.e. Mēr) is spelt in the varsified section as Maihira and interpreted as ‘the descendant of the Sun-god (Mihira).’ The genealogy given in the record is the same as in No. 209 above, but mentions Vijala under the name Vaijala and includes the names of the wives of Mukaṁda, Dhanā and Balarāja. The excavation of the step-well was done by Vanā, son of sūtradhāra Rājā, and Khētā, son of sūtradhāra Dēvadāsa, who are the same as Vanāka and Khētāka in No. 209 above.

Place

Dynasty
Chālukya of Kalyāṇa.
King
Vikramāditya VI

Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records a grant of 15 mattar of land for the god Rēvaṇēśvara by the queen Suggaladēvi at the request of Nāgarāja of the Vāji family, whose genealogy is described in the record. It is stated that the queen made a grant of land belonging to Nāgarahāḷ for the Brahmapuri on the occasion of the installation-of the deity, Śiva Svaya-mbhu, by Rebbaladēvi, wife of Kalichōra. The same village is stated to have been granted for god Rēvaṇēśvara and for the Brāhmaṇas, by Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Eṟeyamarasa.

Written by Bhāva and engraved by Nāgadēva. In characters of about the 10th century. Noticed by Cunningham, ASR, Vol. VII, pp. 50-51; published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXV, pp. 171 ff.

The assignment is stated to have been made on the occasion of a lunar eclipse.

ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/395 (page 86)
Place
Slab set up inside the Ādinātha Basti
Dynasty
Kalachurya
King
Bijjaḷa
Date
Śaka 1087 (current), Tāraṇa, Phālguna śu. 13, Thursday = 1165 A.D., February 25.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records a gift of land, house-site for a dānaśālā, garden etc., for worship, offerings etc., to the Nēminātha basadi at Ekka-saṁbuge situated in Koravaḷḷi-gampanāḍu of Kūṇḍi pro-vince, by Kārtavīrya of the Raṭṭa family. The basadi was got built by Kāḷaṇa, a subordinate of Vijayāditya of the Śilāhāra dynasty who was ruling from his capital at Vaḷavāḍa. He made an endowment in favour of the basadi and entrusted it to mahā-maṇḍalāchārya Vijayakīrti of Yāpanīyasaṅgha and Punnāgavṛikshamūlagaṇa. The record contains genealogical accounts of Kāḷaṇa, Kārtavīrya and Vijayāditya. It further registers gifts of income from taxes etc., to the same basadi by the five hundred svāmis of Ayyāvoḷe, the 1700 gavaṟes, mummuridaṇḍas, taḷa-samasta and ubhaya-nānādēśis. Noticed in Mys. Arch. Reports, 1916, pp. 48-50.

Damaged, worn out and incomplete. The king is stated to be ruling from a village (kuppa ?) on the banks of the river Gautamī. The record refers to an encounter between the king and a certain Bhillama, probably of the Yādava family. Also mentions Bammidēva. Records that Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Allahulidēva of the Kār-ttavīrya family, ruler of Sagara-500, built the temple of god Kannēśvara in the name of his father Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Kannarasa, and made grants for the renovation of the temple and for offering worship etc., to the deity.

RAICHUR DISTRICT


KOPPAL TALUK


ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/483 (page 97)
Place
Munirābād.--Slab in the temple of Śiva.
Dynasty
Chālukya of Kalyāṇa
King
Tribhuvanamalla, ruling from Kalyāṇa
Date
Chālukya-Vikrama 13, Vibhava, Chaitra (wrong for Vaiśākha) śu. Akshayatritīyā, Monday, saṁ-krānti = 1088 A.D., March 27, f.d.t. ·30.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records a grant of land by Sōmēśvarabhaṭṭa, the ūroḍeya of Pulige (also called Vyāghra-grāma) and his wife Mañchikabbe to the god Sōmēśvara installed by them. Another grant of land and garden to the same deity made by the fiftytwo mahājanas of the place is also recorded. Specified shares in the income from grant-land were allotted to the worshipping Brāhmaṇa, the bhaṭṭa reciting the purāṇa in the presence of the god and two temple attendants. It was enjoined that rice, ghee, betel-leaves and nuts, etc. for the offerings to the god should be provided from out of the same income. Similar provisions were made for the repairs of the temple and for a satra to feed twelve Brāhmaṇas. A supplementary grant made on a saṅkramaṇa of the year Parābhava is referred to on the top portion of the stone. Published in Hyderabad Archaeolo-gical Series, No. 5.

Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa

The latter is praised as being worshipped by Tribbuvanamalla and other kings.

ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/540 (page 101)
Place
Do.

Chāhamāna of Nāḍōl
King
Kēlhaṇadēva
Date
Vikrama 1236, Kār-ttika śu. 1, Wed-nesday = 1179 A.D., October 3.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
States that when the king's son Kumarasiṁha was in charge of Māṇḍavyapura, and when Kīrtipāla was his Rājyavā-haka Rājasēvaka Vishayi Dhārāvarsha of Guhila-gōtra made a vyavasthā in the presence of the Sachchikādēvī-gōshṭhikas. The vyavasthā seems to be that each of the bhōjakas should keep watch at the gate of the Sachchikādēvī temple for one prahara and get one karsha, etc., every day from the kōsh-ṭhāgāra of the temple. Published in Jaina Inscriptions Pt., I, p. 198. Cf. Bhandarkar's List, No. 384.

ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/593 (page 106)
Place
Slab fixed above the interior door of the Ādinātha temple.
Dynasty
Mughal
King
Akbar
Date
Vikrama 1661, Mārgaśira śu. 5, Thursday, Uttarāshāḍhā-nak-shatra = 1604 A.D., November 15.
Language & Alphabet
Local dialect, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the installation of Padmaśilā in the temple of Ādinātha, by Sāhu śrī-Kuṁbhā on the advice of his guru Jaśah2-Kīrti, in the presence of his sons and grandsons. Also records the construction of the chaity-ālaya by his sons Sāhu Jitamalla and Nāthamalla. Kuṁbhā belonged to Khaṇḍēlavāla family. Mention is made of mahārājādhirāja Rāisalaji of Kūrma family and the minister (pradhāna) Dēidāsajī. Noticed in A.R. Rajputana Museum, 1935, p. 5, No. XI.

SIROHI DISTRICT


SIROHI TAHSIL


ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/596 (page 107)
Place
Barlūṭ.--Stone slab in three pieces kept in the compound of the Śāntinātha temple.
Dynasty
Chāhamāna of Sōṅ-girā.
King
(1) Mahārāṇaka Udayasiṁha (2) Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Chāchigadēva
Date
(1) Vikrama 1283, Jyēshṭha śu. 8, Thursday = 1226 A.D., May 7, (the tithi was śu. 9). (2) Vikrama 1330, Phālguna śu. 11, Sunday = 1274 A.D., February 18.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Contains two records. (1) Mentions Āśarāja of Naḍūla, his son Ālhaṇa, his son Gajasiṁha of Maṇḍōra, his son Mana-ṇasiṁha and also Yaśōdhīra who was the minister of Udaya-siṁha. Records that Rāja Ābhaṭa, son of Āsaṭa who belonged to the paṭṭa of Manaṇasiṁha made a gift of land to the deity Sāntinātha and to the Manaṇasiṁha-vihāra and a pīṭha in the village Valadaüṭha to the god Śāntinātha for the merit of Manaṇasiṁha. Also records that Rāja Ābhaṭa, along with his sons, made a gift of one dramma for the pūjā of the same deity. (2) Records that the Manaṇasiṁhavihāra was constructed by Rāja Ābhaṭa and his sons for the merit of Rā.º Manaṇa-siṁha. A supplementary record at the end states that a Śrēº (Śrēshṭhin) named Padma-iṁha of the Prāgvāṭa community built a temple along with the members of his family and that his work was consecrated by Guṇabhadra sūri, disciple of Dha-nēśvara-sūri belonging to the Santāna of Sarvadēv-āchārya of Bṛihad-gachchha. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXVI, pp. 33 ff.

ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/662 (page 114)
Place
Chīrwā.--Stone inscription. Impression through the Superintendent, Depart-ment of Archaeology, Western Circle, Baroda.
Dynasty
Guhila
King
Samarasiṁha
Date
Vikrama 1330, Kārttika śu. pra-tipad, Friday = 1273 A.D., October 13.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Traces the royal genealogy from Bappaka. Speaks of the services and valour of some members of the Ṭāṁṭaraḍa com-munity. They are--Uddharaṇa; his son Yōgarāja; his three sons Pamarāja, Mahēndra and Kshēma; Mahēndra's son Bālāka and his sons Ratna and Madana. Ratnaprabhasūri of the Chaitra gachchha, who was revered by Viśvaladēva and Tējasiṁha, composed the praśasti. It was written by his pupil, Pārśvachandra. Kēlisiṁha, son of Padmasiṁha, engraved it, with further help from the śilpin Dēlhaṇa. Pub-lished in Vienna Oriental Journal, Vol. XXI, pp. 155 ff. See Bhandarkar's List, No. 579.

PAKISTAN, EAST


RAJSHAHI DISTRICT


ARIE/1959-1960/B/1959-60/754 (page 122)
Place
Bhaturiā.--Stone slab in the mosque. a Photograph from the authorities of the Varēndra Research Society, Rajshahi.
Dynasty
Pāla of Bengal
King
Rājyapāla
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Gauḍīya
Remarks
Records the erection of a temple surrounded by eight other shrines and installation therein of the god Vṛishabhadhvaja in his Liṅga form by Yaśōdāsa, who bore the designation of Sachiva, and was made Mantrin and Tantrādhikārin by king Rājyapāla, also mentioned as Rāmaparākrama. Records also that the king (Rājyapāla) dedicated the village of Ma-dhuśrava in favour of the god installed by Yaśōdāsa after having fixed the nikara at one hundred Purāṇas (apparently per annum). Also mentions the locality called Aṭṭamūla, which originally formed a part of Bṛihaddhaṭṭa and was the home of the Dāsa family (from which came Yaśōdāsa). The name of the engraver was Śrīnidhāna. Published in IHQ, Vol. XXXI, pp. 215 ff.; Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXIII, pp. 150 ff.
